  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_70a5fd2f-ec1e-43e3-a13c-3cedb49a881e'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer3054890995985846322">Twenty years ago, Claire Maloney was the willful, pampered, tomboyish daughter of the town's most respected family, but that didn't stop her from befriending Roan Sullivan, a fierce, motherless boy who lived in a rusted-out trailer amid junked cars. No one in Dunderry, Georgia--least of all Claire's family--could understand the bond between these two mavericks. But Roan an</span>
  <span id="freeText3054890995985846322" style="display:none">Twenty years ago, Claire Maloney was the willful, pampered, tomboyish daughter of the town's most respected family, but that didn't stop her from befriending Roan Sullivan, a fierce, motherless boy who lived in a rusted-out trailer amid junked cars. No one in Dunderry, Georgia--least of all Claire's family--could understand the bond between these two mavericks. But Roan and Claire belonged together...until the dark afternoon when violence and terror overtook them, and Roan disappeared from Claire's life. Now, two decades later, Claire is adrift, and the Maloneys are still hoping the past can be buried under the rich Southern soil. But Roan Sullivan is about to walk back into their lives....<br /><br />By turns tender and sexy and heartbreaking and exuberant, A Place to Call Home is an enthralling journey between two hearts--and a deliciously original novel from one of the most imaginative and appealing new voices in Southern fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3054890995985846322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Katherine Coble" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/295586-katherine-coble"><img alt="Katherine Coble" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424895309p2/295586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/466431289?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine Coble" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine Coble" href="/user/show/295586-katherine-coble">Katherine Coble</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer466431289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14427012650421453931">QUIT COMPARING THIS TO _SWEET GUM TREE._<br/><br/>I swear. So many reviewers are holding this book in disdainful comparison to Allred's novel, yet no one seems to note that Smith's version came out almost a decade before _Sweet Gum Tree_. I won't say that Allred ripped Smith off, but I'll say that I'm pretty miffed at everyone acting like Smith's book is the carbon copy of Allred's. I think she's an amazing storyteller (no, I don't know her personally) but I have yet to meet any novelist who is able to pl</span>
  <span id="freeText14427012650421453931" style="display:none">QUIT COMPARING THIS TO _SWEET GUM TREE._<br /><br />I swear. So many reviewers are holding this book in disdainful comparison to Allred's novel, yet no one seems to note that Smith's version came out almost a decade before _Sweet Gum Tree_. I won't say that Allred ripped Smith off, but I'll say that I'm pretty miffed at everyone acting like Smith's book is the carbon copy of Allred's. I think she's an amazing storyteller (no, I don't know her personally) but I have yet to meet any novelist who is able to plaigerise a work written ten years AFTER hers. <br /><br />Yes, I love this book. I love everything about it, including the fact that there is a huge cast of characters. In a book where "family" is the central theme it's nice to have there be, you know, a big family. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14427012650421453931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/731296656" />
    <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired"><img alt="Rashika (is tired)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476647072p2/8492956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=why-did-i-read-it">why-did-i-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=adult">adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer731296656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12124171228515275210"><b> Actual Rating 2.5 </b><br/><br/>THIS IS A RANT<br/><br/>I read this book on a hunch really (I am not even sure if that's the right way to put it) and honestly it just didn't pan out. I just wanted a little light/fun romance to balance out the other 4 books I was reading at the moment. <br/><br/>So there are two parts to the book, the first part-the past and the second-the present. The past was perfect. I really thought I was on to something and that I had made a good choice when I decided to read the book. The portrayal of this</span>
  <span id="freeText12124171228515275210" style="display:none"><b> Actual Rating 2.5 </b><br /><br />THIS IS A RANT<br /><br />I read this book on a hunch really (I am not even sure if that's the right way to put it) and honestly it just didn't pan out. I just wanted a little light/fun romance to balance out the other 4 books I was reading at the moment. <br /><br />So there are two parts to the book, the first part-the past and the second-the present. The past was perfect. I really thought I was on to something and that I had made a good choice when I decided to read the book. The portrayal of this young innocent child in love was beautiful. I wasn't skeptic at all (which is somewhat of a surprise). Deborah really pulled her character off. I mean even the part when she first finds out about sex (I had to mention it). Yes I really loved her reaction because it reminded me of mine so I connected with this young child. What amazes me even more is how the author portrayed Roanie's feelings for Claire. Because they had a 5 years age gap (this mattered because she was 9 and he 14... you get my point don't you?), had Roanie felt anything sexual towards Claire, that would have been completely wrong in my book. The author takes a different spin on his feelings, they aren't brotherly but they aren't sexual either they have a hint of romantic but really she was the one person who saw beyond everything else and to him instead of all the other B.S.. so she meant the world to him, he would have done anything for her. <br /><br />After a while though the past just seemed too long to me, I wanted to get to the present and see their reunion and how things worked out. Well umm Ugh? Yeah that was my reaction to the present part of the book. It was extremely disappointing. After everything she had built up in the past, how she played the whole thing was just a big fat disappointment. <br /><br />For starters I didn't even like Roanie until near the end. He gave me the willies. Now I don't care what anyone else says but what he was doing was stalking. He knew everything about her, he had his people and inside contacts find things out. He once even went as far as to be parked outside her dorm and watch her. If that isn't stalking I don't know what the hell is. It was just extremely disturbing. Don't try to justify what he did with his feelings. A lot of creepy stalkers will think they love the person they are stalking so you cannot really make it sound any better, at least not to me. It is just not romantic. Hell if he loved her so much he might have contacted her at least once in the past 20 years. Aside from his stalker tendencies (for which he really should get checked) I hated how immature Roanie was acting. He was flaunting his money around and went as far as to try to buy Claire (at least that's what it seemed like to me). He never even tried to understand why Claire was so vary of the whole thing and fighting him! Where did the Roanie I grew to love from the past go??<br /><br /><b>(spoilers start here)</b><br /><br />Let is move on to the ungrateful bastard, Matthew. WOW. I cannot believe how easily he turned on the man who had raised him. I really cannot. So Josh tells him that he has been looking for him for the past 20 years and he just falls for that? What about the time when the same guy denied his existence and was ashamed of him? Huh? I just. I just. UGH! <br /><br />And now the biggest bastard of all, Josh. I absolutely hated how Deborah played Josh. First the surprise that he was actually the father and then the fact that the author tried to tell us that he wasn't all that bad and had been looking for his lost son and was worried about him? Someone shoot him in the head for me pretty please? Never mind that he denied the existence of his child and let him stay in those horrible conditions for the first few years of his life. He also ignored his legitimate child because of this. The poor girl thought her father hated her for the first 10 years of her fucking life. Oh lets not forget he took advantage of an underage girl. Someone who treats a woman like that isn't worthy of any respect and don't you dare give me the Vietnam excuse. Look at Grandpa Joe if you need any reason as to why I won't accept that bullshit. <br /><br />I am just disappointed. At least I have Castle and The Dream Thieves to cheer me up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12124171228515275210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_808127452" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/808127452" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/808127452?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12287093-a-place-to-call-home">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=kids-in-plot">kids-in-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=heartwarming">heartwarming</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer808127452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer808339385882626158"><b> 3.75 stars for the book; 3 stars for the audio. </b> In many scenes comparable to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2761356.The_Sweet_Gum_Tree' title='The Sweet Gum Tree by Katherine Allred' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sweet Gum Tree</a>, this is angsty women's fiction or chick-lit focused on family drama in an Irish community in Georgia. Fierce childhood devotion becomes adult passion, but the developing romance often takes a back seat to the family drama. <br/><br/>The story is told in two equally divided parts, spanning 25 years, from about 1970 to 1995. It's told in 1st person by the heroine, first as a little girl, then as an adult, with</span>
  <span id="freeText808339385882626158" style="display:none"><b> 3.75 stars for the book; 3 stars for the audio. </b> In many scenes comparable to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2761356.The_Sweet_Gum_Tree" title="The Sweet Gum Tree by Katherine Allred" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sweet Gum Tree</a>, this is angsty women's fiction or chick-lit focused on family drama in an Irish community in Georgia. Fierce childhood devotion becomes adult passion, but the developing romance often takes a back seat to the family drama. <br /><br />The story is told in two equally divided parts, spanning 25 years, from about 1970 to 1995. It's told in 1st person by the heroine, first as a little girl, then as an adult, with some wonderful letters portraying the POV of the hero, first as an adolescent, later as a man. <br /><br />Contents: A few fade-to-black sex scenes, some swearing, some violence, sexual violence, a few typos. <br /><br /><b>Audio narration by Kymberly Dakin.</b> Her voice is easy on the ears and most of the characters sounded tolerably Southern and distinct enough. However, I could hear it whenever she drew a deep breath. Also, the adult Roan sounded too much like his younger self. His voice lacked firmness, texture, depth. Also, Dakin mispronounced "malevolent" every time, and also said "stifled" wrong. In general, the narration is fine.<br /><br />Book, in two parts:<br /><b> PART ONE, 4.5 stars, childhood.</b> The author portrays young Roanie Sullivan and little Claire Maloney, a Georgia peach, unspoiled and honest, even though she is the town princess. Roanie is dirt poor, the neglected "trailer trash" son of an abusive, drunken snake. He lives in Sullivan's Hollow, bordering her family's prosperous chicken farm. He is honorable, and fiercely protective of Claire. I liked part one, portraying the utter loyalty and devotion between the two kids. Only Claire believes in Roanie, but that's a start, and her friendship and faith changes how others view him. Roanie and his little Peep (Claire) are obviously destined for a soul-deep love. Part one ends with a tragic occurrence, when Roan is 15 and Claire is 10. The two are separated and do not meet again for 20 years.<br /><br /><b>PART TWO, 2.5 stars, adulthood. </b> After several chapters about a secondary character, and several letters from Roan to Claire, the author eventually gets around to Claire and Roan meeting as adults. Their romance gets short shrift, with a rather hasty coming together, and it didn't hit the sweet spot -- and I'm not talking about sex. I wasn't looking for an explicitly sexy read, so didn't miss it. Problem is, their relationship -- which was thoroughly set in cement in childhood -- was partly pushed aside to focus on a few secondary characters. This annoyed me. And worse, I felt that Josh and even Matthew got off too easily. Josh especially. Not enough plot for the adult Roan and Claire, and not enough character development for them. The adult H/h didn't quite have the same deep bond the kids had. Also, too much Maloney family history, and too many descriptions of people that don't matter. For example, why spend so many paragraphs describing the construction crew, and the foreman who liked Motzart? He never appeared in the book again. <br /><br /><b>Bottom line, this is a good story -- and even a feel-good story -- but just a little disappointing. </b> As chick-lit, it did the job. I was bawling like a baby towards the end, during the poignant scenes after the tornado -- the relinquishing of old demons and long-dead ghosts, and the improv sermonette. This book had me in tears, and had me chuckling (but only once or twice), and had me reflecting on some profound themes, like social stigma, forgiveness, justice, and family socialization. It had me outraged for the sake of poor young Roan -- and sometimes for adult Roan. However, the author included far too many secondary characters -- all those damn Maloneys and Delaneys in Dunderry, Georgia. I enjoyed it, but grew impatient with the side stories about other people.<br /><br /> I will try another by this author, someday.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="808339385882626158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2547029942949232955">I found it difficult to rate this book and I'm not even sure why. Maybe it has to do with the fact that I can't even describe how I feel about this book, or maybe, it's because it left me hallow in some ways. I don't know, the only thing I can say is that this book was just... it just was.<br/><br/>Overall, I have to give it a two star rating because of two things. Was this worth a read? And, would I recommend this book to someone else? The answer is no on both counts. There was nothing magical and spell </span>
  <span id="freeText2547029942949232955" style="display:none">I found it difficult to rate this book and I'm not even sure why. Maybe it has to do with the fact that I can't even describe how I feel about this book, or maybe, it's because it left me hallow in some ways. I don't know, the only thing I can say is that this book was just... it just was.<br /><br />Overall, I have to give it a two star rating because of two things. Was this worth a read? And, would I recommend this book to someone else? The answer is no on both counts. There was nothing magical and spell binding about this book, this book was really nothing more than just words on printed page.<br /><br />While, well written, the book was more back-story (family history) than actual story and it got to an exhausting point. It was also heavily-ladened with a little too much description and thus, again, not enough story. I found myself questioning what the plot of the story was and even more, what the heck, the point was of this story.<br /><br />This book had me in tears in certain parts, had me laughing in others, but overall, it just lacked. Lacked. Not enough romance, not enough story, not enough true character depth, just deep-rooted family history and pain. It was okay.</span>

<div id="review_380001426" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380001426" />
    <a title="Aarati" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5788891-aarati"><img alt="Aarati" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504633885p2/5788891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380001426?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aarati" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aarati" href="/user/show/5788891-aarati">Aarati</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer2457373501332730071">I read this because I heard about the similarities to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2761356.The_Sweet_Gum_Tree' title='The Sweet Gum Tree by Katherine Allred' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sweet Gum Tree</a> and wanted to compare the two stories for myself. Even though the premise was extremely similar, the characters were distinct and the direction the stories took after the childhood-sweethearts-stage was different.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, while I enjoyed the first section of this story (I love the Southern small town setting!), the book dragged for me when Roan and Claire reunited as adults. I wasn't especially interested in the hundreds </span>
  <span id="freeText2457373501332730071" style="display:none">I read this because I heard about the similarities to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2761356.The_Sweet_Gum_Tree" title="The Sweet Gum Tree by Katherine Allred" rel="nofollow noopener">Sweet Gum Tree</a> and wanted to compare the two stories for myself. Even though the premise was extremely similar, the characters were distinct and the direction the stories took after the childhood-sweethearts-stage was different.<br /><br />Unfortunately, while I enjoyed the first section of this story (I love the Southern small town setting!), the book dragged for me when Roan and Claire reunited as adults. I wasn't especially interested in the hundreds of pages of family drama (the romance was essentially resolved in the middle of the book). I also found it strange that Roan stalked Claire for years but never even contacted her once - she'd never rejected him, and I was irritated that he used Matthew as an excuse to stay away from the Maloneys. The second half of the book was only 2 stars for me but the first part was so outstanding that I couldn't rate this less than 4 stars.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammicco" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammicco" href="/user/show/8701810-tammicco">Tammicco</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer657799192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11277943085101486601">I love the mature writing in this story. We get hues of a rich history and culture back-lighted by a youthful loyalty come romance between the H/h. This book is more about that history and culture than the romance, per se, but I'm only interested in that history and culture as it relates to the romance. I doubt I would have bought into the harshness of the H's character had I not had the background laid out so thoroughly. This is damn fine writing.<br/><br/>I read Sweet Gum Tree first and this book was am</span>
  <span id="freeText11277943085101486601" style="display:none">I love the mature writing in this story. We get hues of a rich history and culture back-lighted by a youthful loyalty come romance between the H/h. This book is more about that history and culture than the romance, per se, but I'm only interested in that history and culture as it relates to the romance. I doubt I would have bought into the harshness of the H's character had I not had the background laid out so thoroughly. This is damn fine writing.<br /><br />I read Sweet Gum Tree first and this book was among those recommended for readers of SGT. I really enjoyed SGT, but I admit that I loved APtoCH much more. I really appreciate mature characterizations, and APtoCH does that more successfully (whereas SGT played to a younger audience, imho). SGT had more of an arrested development in its heroine that was not enjoyable at certain points during my reading--read more like an old fashioned Harlequin Romance at times. <br /><br />Anyway both books were incredible reads, but APtoCH feeds something in me. It takes the innocent, the jaded, the harsh, the abusive, the redeemable, the celebratory, and makes something that's home-made and real for me (being as I'm from the south, and all). It felt like so much more than just a story. It renewed me. I can't ask more from a book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11277943085101486601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102813927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer933557922459879174">I randomly picked up this book at the library and I loved it. I was so drawn to both Claire and Roan's character from the very beginning as I saw their relationship throughout their childhood to adulthood. <br/><br/>The first part of the book was so captivating and emotional. I couldn't put it down. Claire is so determined to help save Roanie Sullivan, despite his unfortunate luck of being born into the wrong family. The two of them are young children and share the kind of love that is unique between the </span>
  <span id="freeText933557922459879174" style="display:none">I randomly picked up this book at the library and I loved it. I was so drawn to both Claire and Roan's character from the very beginning as I saw their relationship throughout their childhood to adulthood. <br /><br />The first part of the book was so captivating and emotional. I couldn't put it down. Claire is so determined to help save Roanie Sullivan, despite his unfortunate luck of being born into the wrong family. The two of them are young children and share the kind of love that is unique between the two of them. It's not sexual, after all they are only children. I just loved Roan. He was always so sweet to Claire from the first day they met. Claire was so young and naive but I loved her will and determination when it came to Roanie Sullivan. <br /><br />The second part of the book takes place years later when both Claire and Roan are adults. The love they shared as children is stronger than ever and nothing, not even a family secret, will keep them apart. You see Roanie go full circle and finally find a place where he belongs. This was the first booked read by Smith and it surely will not be my last. </span>
  <a data-text-id="933557922459879174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText850995386347655639" style="display:none"><i>"I planned to be the kind of old Southern lady who talked to her tomato plants and bought sweaters for her cats. I'd just turned thirty, but I was already sizing up where I'd been and where I was headed. So I knew that when I was old I would be deliberately peculiar"</i><br /><br /><b>Ms. Smith...you really did a number on me. 5 bright, sparkling stars!</b><br /><br />Let's take a journey with Claire Maloney in her home town of Dunderry, Georgia where at the mere age of 10 years old, she dares to defy the elitist standards of her family and befriend the son of town's local outcast - Roanie Sullivan.<br /><br />Claire is by far the world's most lovable child - displaying childhood innocence with enough edge to let the reader know that she not only believes in all things good in the world, but she's willing to fight to keep them that way. Her persistence in befriending Roanie Sullivan despite everything in her DNA that all but requires her to stay away from his type is what ultimately steals your heart and makes you fall in love with Claire and all she stands for. And we're not the only ones falling in love with her...<br /><br />The odds were inevitably against Roanie from the start. And being the son of Big Roan Sullivan doesn't make Roanie's life any easier in the town of Dunderry. It's no wonder why he's hell bent on rejecting anything good that may come his way. In Roanie's life, anything good eventually comes to a disastrous end...that is, until he meets Claire...<br /><br />Claire and Roan's story of friendship and love is the stuff that all romances should be made of. Their bond that carries the two of them from their childhood to adulthood is ultimately what will keep you turning the page. <br /><br />Another thing I have to mention is how appreciative I am of the author for keeping some mystery in the love scenes. These days it just seems like romance authors are so determined to just over sexualize a love scene in a desperate attempt to fall in line with age old theory that "sex sells". Well maybe it's just me, but in the era of 50 Shades of Grey once you've read one sex scene, you've read them all. I usually just skip them anyway, so I appreciated Smith not letting the scenes drag on and on to the point where I'm rolling my eyes and skipping pages. Granted, I realize this book was published in the late 90's, but again - unrealistic and overdramatized sex is not a new trend. Thank you for keeping it real Deborah.<br /><br />You will feel betrayed, you will feel angry, you will be shocked, and you will feel heartbreak as you continue to see just how many forces try to break Claire and Roan apart. But, like any great romance - in the end love prevails. Bravo Smith. Well done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="850995386347655639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15215727611021544993">This was a sprawling, Southern, spitfire of an epic and I loved every witticism, foxglove petal, and scandal within it. A tale that explores family and friendship, with one of the best love stories I've ever read. I admired how real it was - the dialogue, the shame, the yearning - and how the story went beyond the romance and HEA to explore loose ends and give everyone their moment.   <span id="freeText15215727611021544993" style="display:none">This was a sprawling, Southern, spitfire of an epic and I loved every witticism, foxglove petal, and scandal within it. A tale that explores family and friendship, with one of the best love stories I've ever read. I admired how real it was - the dialogue, the shame, the yearning - and how the story went beyond the romance and HEA to explore loose ends and give everyone their moment. Lots of metaphor and symbolism and gorgeous description, and class discrimination. In many ways, it echoed "To Kill A Mockingbird" or "Dandelion Wine", but with a dash of love and a rags-to-riches storyline. What a complete surprise. I'll always remember reading this on my first Thanksgiving as a newlywed &lt;3 I hope Ms. Smith's other novels are of the same caliber.</span>

    <a title="Susannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1352895-susannah"><img alt="Susannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442961763p2/1352895.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553103342" href="/book/show/2115683.A_Place_to_Call_Home">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1352895-susannah?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1352895-susannah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130810393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6841935883480505368">This book was a lovely, complex read. It is hard for me to find romance stories that I can actually get past the first couple of pages; for every one I pick up, I've put down ten others. Nevertheless, I really enjoy the good ones so I keep looking for those jewels among the dross. Deborah Smith's novel "A Place To Call Home" was everything I look for in this type of book: a rich, intelligently developed plot peopled with characters who are not only interesting but don't do ridiculous things mere</span>
  <span id="freeText6841935883480505368" style="display:none">This book was a lovely, complex read. It is hard for me to find romance stories that I can actually get past the first couple of pages; for every one I pick up, I've put down ten others. Nevertheless, I really enjoy the good ones so I keep looking for those jewels among the dross. Deborah Smith's novel "A Place To Call Home" was everything I look for in this type of book: a rich, intelligently developed plot peopled with characters who are not only interesting but don't do ridiculous things merely for the sake of the dramatic outcome, as well as realistic and well-written dialogue, sub-plots, and side characters who are just as interesting as the main ones. Oh, and a believable connection between the romantic partners - you can easily understand and support why they are who they are and do what they do, without having to make that leap of faith so often necessary for most romantic reads just to be able to get to "the good parts." <br /><br />It's just really wonderful to see who Roan and Claire became, and how they each brought the best in each other to the surface. Forgiveness and human connection are adeptly woven into the story which makes it all the more satisfying. I highly recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6841935883480505368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_292470527" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292470527" />
    <a title="Sharon Dodge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4707001-sharon-dodge"><img alt="Sharon Dodge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293572592p2/4707001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292470527?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon Dodge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon Dodge" href="/user/show/4707001-sharon-dodge">Sharon Dodge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292470527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18175765524903696944">Another rare creature: a romance novel that's genuinely good. Oddly, it's the lead-up, not the actual romance between the adult characters in the somewhat hasty and strange last quarter of the book, that caught me. I've always felt when you buy a romance novel, you should get a romance novel; I loathe romances that focus so much on the dramatic setting or murder mystery you hardly notice the romance. But in this novel, I felt the reverse.<br/><br/>The story is at its best at the start, when the plucky 5-y</span>
  <span id="freeText18175765524903696944" style="display:none">Another rare creature: a romance novel that's genuinely good. Oddly, it's the lead-up, not the actual romance between the adult characters in the somewhat hasty and strange last quarter of the book, that caught me. I've always felt when you buy a romance novel, you should get a romance novel; I loathe romances that focus so much on the dramatic setting or murder mystery you hardly notice the romance. But in this novel, I felt the reverse.<br /><br />The story is at its best at the start, when the plucky 5-year-old heroine sticks up for the town scamp - a child not much older that is dirty, poor, and the son of the town's meanest drunk, an old man who leers out of the book's pages with surprising strength. Over the course of several years, they become inseparable, to the point the girl's (wealthy, well-respected family) takes in the boy. It's a chaste, childish romance, but a powerful one all the less. My only regret is that the separation that subsequently occurs lasts so long; by the time they meet again, they aren't the children you know at all, and it's hard to feel the same powerful connection when twenty years, education, and success have so radically changed them both. <br /><br />But still, it's a dear, fun novel, and for a romance, one of the very best.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18175765524903696944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3315174917" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3315174917" />
    <a title="Infantina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/110166636-infantina"><img alt="Infantina" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3315174917?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Infantina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Infantina" href="/user/show/110166636-infantina">Infantina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/110166636-infantina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3315174917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9673872932867651073"><br/>I am disappointed with myself for not reviewing this book sooner. There's no point mulling over a past mistake. I am righting a wrong at this hour which you can see. The fact is I picked up this great novel from my college library , my second home back in 2011. If truth be told, this is one of the elegant story that I will cherish in my heart for a lifetime.<br/><br/>The novel has solid footing with a huge family tree and an embellished history about the ancestors of the female lead which is enough to hoo</span>
  <span id="freeText9673872932867651073" style="display:none"><br />I am disappointed with myself for not reviewing this book sooner. There's no point mulling over a past mistake. I am righting a wrong at this hour which you can see. The fact is I picked up this great novel from my college library , my second home back in 2011. If truth be told, this is one of the elegant story that I will cherish in my heart for a lifetime.<br /><br />The novel has solid footing with a huge family tree and an embellished history about the ancestors of the female lead which is enough to hook the readers and keep them in the edge of their seats. A reader is introduced to innumerable characters . No scepticism occurs though which is gratifying. It's something that puts a huge smile on my face. What better way than describe about one's honorable family of generations and their heritage.<br /><br />The ones who are dissecting this book will be on an emotional plane to get a whole picture about their family background and most interestingly, will try to rule out everything regarding their ancestors to their existing family members. I did it. I don't know if you'd be hypnotized.<br /><br />Claire Karleene Maloney is the female protagonist while Roanie Sullivan is the male protagonist. The voice of the story is Claire. First half is about the blossoming of innocent love of a small girl for the motherless, ugly, badtoothed sinister looking teenager.<br /><br />This is a rich, beautiful girl falls in love with a shabby, poor boy kinda story. I presume you may have read or watched plenty of this type a lot. But this is something outside the box. A sacred bond love story of one in a million. There's magic in author's imagination. The first half captivated my mind aesthetically.<br /><br />Claire is warned by many in her family to stay apart from Roanie. She is certainly unique and doesn't care about the opinions of others and say least let them dictate what she should or shouldn't do.<br /><br />I liked the manner how she cared for the teenage boy. He doesn't like charity despite his unstable, horrible, better die than live situation. She implores his heart to make him perceive she is nothing but his pure-intended friend. He gets it in due course.<br /><br />Circumstances make Roanie work in her house. They mingle well. Her family find that he is unlike his father who is a sexual predator and an alcoholic. Since the first part is about the relationship between childhood sweethearts, the romance is subtle and heartwarmimg. There's no sexual tension for they are young.<br /><br />Roanie is a grownup teenager who is mature and well-read beyond his age. He considers her as his angel who he swears to protect from harm's intent and likewise, she. Everything goes in the right direction until the fate shocks them. The big Roan tries to rape the 10 year old girl. What happens next?<br /><br />The second half takes after 20 years. Claire is now 30 years old and has become a journalist like she desired when she was small. 35 years old Roanie, on the other hand is a big shot and has made his childhood dream a reality- from rags to riches. Will these two soulmates cross paths and live happily ever after like once they hoped in their hearts decades ago?<br /><br />Vile truths about her family will break Claire's heart. Roanie is very stubborn and wants only her but is not willing to be part of her family clan ever. He holds immense grudges against them all. She thinks otherwise. Mathew, the 24 year old who he raised since the young man was less than 5 years old with superabundant love betrays him and unites with Claire's family leaving his ego bruised and heart broken.<br /><br />Can Roanie get back the love of Mathew who he viewed as his own blood , sacrificed his heart's desires and most part of his life for the young man's sake? Claire, supports him in the tougher times and take vows to make Mathew and his wife understand Roanie , a strong, decent and gentle soul.<br /><br />The author is poised to the maximum.<br />She has a way with words. My special liking goes for the wondrous first half which is flawless according to my perception. Although the story plot of the second half was good, Ms. Deborah Smith has failed to deliver it perfectly like I wished. I blame it on her lethargic writing skills.<br /><br />More family members, more messes. Few family members, few messes . This kept on ringing in my mind after I finished her book. Contrarywise, when lacking the support of family members, the turbulent phase one goes through in their life cannot be overcome. I had mixed insights about the book. Teenager Roanie sprung me. Who wouldn't actually? Not liking him involves an arduous process. He is one of my book boyfriends.<br /><br />Overall, I am enigmatically astonished by Deborah Smith's one of the gems.'A place to call home' is worth reading. You can as well as choose to read the first half which found a permanent place in many readers heart just like me and will not vanish as long as another brilliant writer comes along and replaces Ms. Deborah Smith's master piece.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9673872932867651073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9922426117227051231" style="display:none">Format: kindle ebook<br />Tissue warning: there's a few sniffly spots<br />HEA: yes<br />Triggers: almost rape<br />Narrative: 1st person, following Claire <br />My reviewer rating: 4.5 out of 5<br />Recommend read: yes<br />Published: May 4th 1998<br /><br />I have a feeling I may come back and edit my rating on this the more I think about it.<br /><br />I loved the writing in this story. Maybe not two authors, but the same author with two different stories. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The first part made me feel as though Roan was helpless and fragile and pitiful. <div id="review_2817761261" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2817761261" />
    <a title="Valerie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47502857-valerie"><img alt="Valerie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465339556p2/47502857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2817761261?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie" href="/user/show/47502857-valerie">Valerie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2817761261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16521669208839840006">So many characters in here, from family members to friends to acquaintances and enemies. Too many to keep track of them all, which is a shame because it made me skim those long passages where a bunch of random characters are mentioned. There were just too many.<br/><br/>Speaking of skimming, there’s so much filler... the first part is all about when they were kids and I usually LOVE books with a lot of background and history between the MCs but here? Sheesh. Random things are mentioned that contribute not</span>
  <span id="freeText16521669208839840006" style="display:none">So many characters in here, from family members to friends to acquaintances and enemies. Too many to keep track of them all, which is a shame because it made me skim those long passages where a bunch of random characters are mentioned. There were just too many.<br /><br />Speaking of skimming, there’s so much filler... the first part is all about when they were kids and I usually LOVE books with a lot of background and history between the MCs but here? Sheesh. Random things are mentioned that contribute nothing to the story. <br /><br />There are a bunch of similarities between this book and “The sweet gum tree”, even in the little details (the heroine thinking she’ll be a writer, or the hero giving a necklace/pendant to the heroine, the hero’s dad being shot, the hero‘s dad being an abusive POS raping young girls, the setting and type of family, etc.). Looking at the publishing dates I can see that “the sweet gum tree” came out years after this one. <br /><br />Still, I can’t help but compare the two since the similarities are endless. The characters in this book are not nearly half as sweet as those in “The sweet gum tree”. The heroine comes across as overbearing in the beginning, and not very likeable. The hero is just very meh, then annoying when he comes back and makes his worthiness dependent on his bank account balance &amp; assets. <br /><br />I’m sad to say I gave up at 70%. Couldn’t take it anymore. Maybe I’d have finished it if I hadn’t read the sweet gum tree right before picking this book, but as it is i did and I couldn’t help compare them, and this one failed miserably.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16521669208839840006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7332789233923538740" style="display:none"><br />Twenty years ago, Claire Maloney was the willful, pampered, tomboyish daughter of the town’s most respected family, but that didn’t stop her from befriending Roan Sullivan, a fierce, motherless boy who lived in a rusted-out trailer amid junked cars. No one in Dunderry, Georgia—least of all Claire’s family–could understand the bond between these two mavericks. But Roan and Claire belonged together . . . until Roans father tried to rape Claire and Roan shot and killed him. Roan was sent to a home but disappeared from Claire’s life. Now, two decades later, Claire is adrift, and the Maloneys are still hoping the past can be buried. It turns out Roam adopted Claire's brother's out of wedlock son and he didn’t come back for Claire until Matthew was grown so the family would not take him away. A lovely romance.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13327844843982222763">(PT em baixo) I just didn’t connect with the characters. Neither with the story. It reminded me of a Nicholas Sparks novel, but less engaging. It is a sweet story and it includes a beautiful loving family (broken but loyal to their family bond despite the difficulties). I wish I could rate it more stars. I don’t because like I said it wasn’t engaging for me and I had to make an effort to read it.<br/>It had some annoying cliches. <br/><br/>Não me consegui ligar aos personagens nem à história.   <span id="freeText13327844843982222763" style="display:none">(PT em baixo) I just didn’t connect with the characters. Neither with the story. It reminded me of a Nicholas Sparks novel, but less engaging. It is a sweet story and it includes a beautiful loving family (broken but loyal to their family bond despite the difficulties). I wish I could rate it more stars. I don’t because like I said it wasn’t engaging for me and I had to make an effort to read it.<br />It had some annoying cliches. <br /><br />Não me consegui ligar aos personagens nem à história. Fez-me lembrar um romance do Nicholas Sparks mas menos apelativo. É uma história querida sobre família e o que chamamos de casa. Gostava de conseguir dar mais estrelas mas na verdade foi aborrecido de ler e tive de me esforçar para chegar ao fim. Tem uns clichês a meu ver irritantes.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2746087482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14428227567242233560">I honestly wanted to love this book, but it came up short for me. I love this genre and long lost loves, but this book hardly kept my attention and I found myself forcing my way through to the end. I'm not going to compare this to The Sweet Gum Tree like most who have read this book have as I do understand that this book came out years before. I will say that if The Sweet Gum Tree was a fan fiction of this book, it won out. I'm just not a fan of the writing and how long and drawn out the author </span>
  <span id="freeText14428227567242233560" style="display:none">I honestly wanted to love this book, but it came up short for me. I love this genre and long lost loves, but this book hardly kept my attention and I found myself forcing my way through to the end. I'm not going to compare this to The Sweet Gum Tree like most who have read this book have as I do understand that this book came out years before. I will say that if The Sweet Gum Tree was a fan fiction of this book, it won out. I'm just not a fan of the writing and how long and drawn out the author made this book. Reading usually is enjoyable for me so forcing myself through this to see what the ending was going to be was painful!</span>

    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pesNKvHWRWMuDG2gJOmGj/Iu3JmJ73gbu+zK7u1OSEYWL3RaS/TXv/j0tI/OFxJg3lbA97VuhT/tn+VG13GJtw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UHdNYME4DNcfxkaaDKiB11VIDFrdCT+vQ/hFpfR2tt3jszQQexqeC8k+n7XmVhU4eTAQNOGIwosVi2oNzkl3LA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14345823690761598864">aka Jackie Leigh<br/>aka Della Stone<br/>aka Leigh Bridger<br/><br/>Bestselling Author<br/>Co-founder, co-publisher<br/>Vice-president, Editor in Chief<br/>BelleBooks, Memphis, TN <br/><br/>Deborah Smith is the New York Times bestselling author of A Place to Call Home, and the No. 1 Kindle Bestseller The Crossroads Cafe, A Gentle Rain and other acclaimed romantic novels portraying life and love in the modern Appalachian South. A native Georg</span>
  <span id="freeText14345823690761598864" style="display:none">aka Jackie Leigh<br />aka Della Stone<br />aka Leigh Bridger<br /><br />Bestselling Author<br />Co-founder, co-publisher<br />Vice-president, Editor in Chief<br />BelleBooks, Memphis, TN <br /><br />Deborah Smith is the New York Times bestselling author of A Place to Call Home, and the No. 1 Kindle Bestseller The Crossroads Cafe, A Gentle Rain and other acclaimed romantic novels portraying life and love in the modern Appalachian South. A native Georgian, Deborah is a former newspaper editor who turned to novel-writing with great success.<br /><br />With more than 35 romance, women's fiction and fantasy novels to her credit, Deborah's books have sold over 3 million copies worldwide. Among her honors is a Lifetime Achievement Award from Romantic Times Magazine and a nomination for the prestigious Townsend Literary Award. In 2003 Disney optioned Sweet Hush for film. In 2008 A Gentle Rain was a finalist in Romance Writers of America's RITA awards.<br /><br />For the past fifteen years Deborah has partnered with Debra Dixon to run BelleBooks, a small press originally known for southern fiction, including the Mossy Creek Hometown Series and the Sweet Tea story collections. As editor, she has worked on projects as diverse as the nonfiction Bra Talk book by three-time Oprah Winfrey guest Susan Nethero, and the In My Dreams novella by New York Times bestselling author Sarah Addison Allen.<br /><br />In 2008 BelleBooks launched Bell Bridge Books, an imprint with a focus on fantasy novels and now expanded to include multi-genre fiction--mystery, suspense, thrillers, women's fiction, nonfiction and other. In 2013 BelleBooks acquired the late Linda Kichline's paranormal romance press, ImaJinn Books, and hired legendary editor Brenda Chin, formerly of Harlequin Books, as editorial director. Chin will expand the imprint to cover a diverse mix of all romance types. <br /> <br />Deborah's newest books are the Crossroads Cafe novellas: THE BISCUIT WITCH, THE PICKLE QUEEN, THE YARN SPINNER, and THE KITCHEN CHARMER (2014). She released a mini-short story, SAVING JONQUILS, in March 2014. A sexy romantic novella, A HARD MAN TO FIND, is scheduled for later in the month.<br /><br /></span>
